</header><div class="entry-content"><input class="jpibfi" type="hidden"/><p><img alt="Grabbing a slice of pizza created using our Gluten-Free Pizza Crust recipe" class="aligncenter wp-image-30776 size-full" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19.jpg" data-pin-description="PERFECT Gluten-Free Pizza Crust! Fluffy, crispy, easy to make, 10 ingredients! #vegan #glutenfree #pizza #recipe #plantbased #minimalistbaker" data-pin-media="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/03/MB-EASY-Vegan-pizza-crust-pinterest.jpg" data-pin-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" height="2184" sizes="(max-width: 960px) 100vw, (max-width: 1149px) 590px, 720px" src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19.jpg" srcset="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19.jpg 1456w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19-600x900.jpg 600w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19-200x300.jpg 200w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19-768x1152.jpg 768w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19-683x1024.jpg 683w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-19-680x1020.jpg 680w" width="1456"/></p>
<p>Friends, it’s here! A <strong>vegan, gluten-free pizza crust</strong> that’s <strong>easy to make</strong> with ingredients you probably have on hand right now. Not to mention, it’s <strong>perfectly crisp on the edges</strong> and firm but tender in the center. Whoop!</p>
<p>Let’s make gluten-free pizza dreams come true!</p>
<p><img alt="Stirring together dry ingredients- almond flour, potato starch, arrowroot starch, flaxseed meal, baking soda, baking soda, and spices for Gluten-Free Vegan Pizza Crust" class="aligncenter wp-image-30777 size-full" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker.jpg" data-pin-description="PERFECT Gluten-Free Pizza Crust! Fluffy, crispy, easy to make, 10 ingredients! #vegan #glutenfree #pizza #recipe #plantbased #minimalistbaker" data-pin-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" height="2184" sizes="(max-width: 960px) 100vw, (max-width: 1149px) 590px, 720px" src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker.jpg" srcset="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker.jpg 1456w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-600x900.jpg 600w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-200x300.jpg 200w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-768x1152.jpg 768w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-683x1024.jpg 683w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-680x1020.jpg 680w" width="1456"/><span id="more-30757"></span></p>
<p>This recipe requires <strong>10 simple ingredients</strong> and comes together in <strong>less than 45 minutes</strong> from start to finish!</p>
<p>The base flours are comprised of almond flour, potato starch, and arrowroot starch. Potato and arrowroot starch are particularly great for this recipe because they help make a firm and crispy-on-the-edges crust that’s also tender in the center.</p>
<p><strong>No gooey center, no cardboard edges – just pure, airy, delicious goodness.</strong></p>
<p><iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="380" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/l5jSDhn5tpI" width="680"></iframe><br/>
<img alt="Stirred together the wet and dry ingredients for our crispy vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" class="aligncenter wp-image-30759 size-full" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2.jpg" data-pin-description="PERFECT Gluten-Free Pizza Crust! Fluffy, crispy, easy to make, 10 ingredients! #vegan #glutenfree #pizza #recipe #plantbased #minimalistbaker" data-pin-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" height="2184" sizes="(max-width: 960px) 100vw, (max-width: 1149px) 590px, 720px" src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2.jpg" srcset="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2.jpg 1456w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2-600x900.jpg 600w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2-200x300.jpg 200w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2-768x1152.jpg 768w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2-683x1024.jpg 683w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-2-680x1020.jpg 680w" width="1456"/></p>
<p>We also included some flaxseed for binding (and fiber), olive oil for moisture (which you can sub for water if oil-free), oregano and garlic for added flavor, and vinegar and baking soda to help the crust rise a bit.</p>
<p>Having tried a lot of gluten-free crusts (our own, at restaurants, and box mixes), we can confidently say this is the best gluten-free pizza crust we’ve tried and SPOT-ON in flavor and texture. Swoon!</p>
<p><img alt="Flattening out the dough for our vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" class="aligncenter wp-image-30761 size-full" data-jpibfi-post-excerpt="" data-jpibfi-post-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" data-jpibfi-post-url="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/" data-jpibfi-src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4.jpg" data-pin-description="PERFECT Gluten-Free Pizza Crust! Fluffy, crispy, easy to make, 10 ingredients! #vegan #glutenfree #pizza #recipe #plantbased #minimalistbaker" data-pin-title="Easy Vegan Gluten-Free Pizza Crust" height="2184" sizes="(max-width: 960px) 100vw, (max-width: 1149px) 590px, 720px" src="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4.jpg" srcset="https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4.jpg 1456w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4-600x900.jpg 600w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4-200x300.jpg 200w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4-768x1152.jpg 768w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4-683x1024.jpg 683w, https://minimalistbaker.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/PERFECT-Gluten-Free-Pizza-Crust-Fluffy-crispy-easy-to-make-10-ingredients-vegan-glutenfree-pizza-recipe-plantbased-minimalistbaker-4-680x1020.jpg 680w" width="1456"/></p>
<p>Once your crust is formed, bake for 10 minutes. Then top with desired toppings. We went for tomato sauce, peppers, onions, mushrooms, kalamata olives, oregano, and <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/whipped-almond-ricotta-5-ingredients/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">whipped almond ricotta cheese</a>. But you could go any way you prefer. I could see <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-pesto-5-minutes/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">pesto</a> working well here, as well as my <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/butternut-squash-veggie-pizza/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">butternut squash sauce</a>!</p>
<p>Just a few more minutes in the oven and it’s officially pizza night!</p>

<p>I hope you all LOVE this crust! It’s:</p>
<p>Easy to make<br/>
Crisp on the edges<br/>
Tender (but firm) in the middle<br/>
Hearty enough to hold LOTS of toppings<br/>
&amp; Insanely delicious!</p>
<p>For those of you in the vegan gluten-free camp, this is <em>thee</em> pizza crust for you. We couldn’t believe how fluffy, crispy, and tender it was all at the same time. Plus, not only is it delicious hot out of the oven, it’s also tasty as leftovers the next day – cold or hot!</p>
<p>If you’re into pizza, also be sure to check out our <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/vegan-portobello-pizzas/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Mini Portobello Pizzas</a>, <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/butternut-squash-veggie-pizza/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Butternut Squash Veggie Pizza</a>, <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/my-favorite-vegan-pizza/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Favorite Vegan Pizza</a>, <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/vegan-cauliflower-pizza-crust/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Cauliflower Pizza Crust</a>, and our original <a href="https://minimalistbaker.com/the-best-gluten-free-pizza-crust-sauce/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">Best Gluten-Free Pizza Crust</a>.</p>
<p>If you try this recipe, let us know! Leave a comment, rate it, and don’t forget to tag a photo <a href="https://www.instagram.com/minimalistbaker/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">#minimalistbaker</a> on Instagram. Cheers, friends!</p>

<h2 class="wprm-recipe-name">Easy Vegan Gluten Free Pizza Crust</h2>
<div class="wprm-recipe-summary">
		An easy-to-make gluten-free pizza crust that's perfectly crisp on the edges and tender in the center. Just 10 ingredients required, easy methods, and so delicious!	</div>

<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Ingredients</h3>
<div class="wprm-unit-conversion-container"><a class="wprm-unit-conversion wprmpuc-active" data-recipe="34158" data-system="1" href="#">US Customary</a> - <a class="wprm-unit-conversion" data-recipe="34158" data-system="2" href="#">Metric</a></div> <div class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-group">

<ul class="wprm-recipe-ingredients">
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1 1/3</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cup</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name"><a href="https://aax-us-east.amazon-adsystem.com/x/c/QhD58smT8fdU70L-DKPftxYAAAFjspI1KwEAAAFKAemBX8U/https://www.amazon.com/dp/B00CLLV2D0/ref=as_at?creativeASIN=B00CLLV2D0&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=G.19ttV8fHXKPz.z25ooUQ&amp;slotNum=0&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20&amp;th=1" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">almond flour</a></span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-notes">(not almond meal // I prefer Wellbee's brand)</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1/2</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cup</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name"><a href="https://aax-us-east.amazon-adsystem.com/x/c/QpkIaeC7R-BRv82WSuAmLPYAAAFjspKbvwEAAAFKAbGyhec/https://www.amazon.com/dp/B0013JOKBC/ref=as_at?creativeASIN=B0013JOKBC&amp;linkCode=w61&amp;imprToken=q31urLwNf0nMVfeECK8fjA&amp;slotNum=18&amp;tag=minimalistbaker-20" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">potato starch</a></span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1/2</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">cup</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">arrowroot starch</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">Tbsp</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">flaxseed meal</span>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-amount">1</span>

</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">

<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">tsp</span>

</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-ingredient">

<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-unit">tsp</span>
<span class="wprm-recipe-ingredient-name">garlic powder</span>
</li>

<div class="wprm-recipe-instructions-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Instructions</h3>
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-group">
<ol class="wprm-recipe-instructions">
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Preheat oven to 375 degrees F (190 C) and line a baking sheet, pizza pan, or pizza stone with parchment paper. (You won't be cooking the pizza on the pan but rather on the parchment paper placed directly on the oven rack. So if you don't have a pizza pan, don't worry. You just need something to hold and transfer the pizza in and out of the oven.)</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">To a medium mixing bowl, add the almond flour, potato starch, arrowroot starch, flaxseed meal, baking soda, oregano, garlic powder, and sea salt and whisk thoroughly to combine.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text"><p>In a separate small mixing bowl, combine the vinegar, olive oil, and water. Whisk to combine.</p></div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Add the wet ingredients to the dry ingredients and stir to combine until a dough forms (see photo). If it's too crumbly, add water until a moldable dough forms. If too wet, add more almond flour.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Transfer the dough to the parchment-lined pan or pizza stone and use your hands (or a floured rolling pin) to flatten and shape into a circle or square (the shape of your pan). It should be about 1/4-inch thick or less. It will puff up a little when baking. If the dough sticks to your hands, lightly oil to prevent sticking.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Transfer the crust to the oven by sliding the crust on the parchment paper onto a middle oven rack and bake for 10 minutes.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Remove the crust with the parchment paper and set it back on the pan or pizza stone. Top with desired sauce and toppings. We went for puréed tomatoes, onion, peppers, oregano, almond ricotta cheese, and kalamata olives (and added sun-dried tomatoes and fresh basil after baking).</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Bake for another 15-20 minutes or until the toppings are toasted and the crust is very slightly golden brown and firm to the touch.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">Enjoy hot! Store leftovers covered in the refrigerator up to 3 days. Enjoy cold, or reheat in a 375-degree oven (190 C) until hot.</div>
</li>
<li class="wprm-recipe-instruction">
<div class="wprm-recipe-instruction-text">To freeze: I would recommend par-baking the crust (completing the initial bake), then freezing on a baking sheet and storing in the freezer up to 6 weeks. Then, bake as instructed, adding a little extra cooking time if baked from frozen.</div>
</li>
</ol>
</div>
</div>

<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Notes</h3>
<p>*Nutrition information is a rough estimate for <strong>1 slice of 6 slices (as the recipe is written)</strong>, crust only without toppings calculated with the oil.</p>
</div>
<div class="wprm-recipe-nutrition-container">
<h3 class="wprm-recipe-header">Nutrition Per Serving (1 of 1 Slice) </h3><ul><li><strong>Calories:</strong> 217 <li><strong>Fat:</strong> 10.6g <li><strong>Saturated fat:</strong> 0.9g <li><strong>Sodium:</strong> 374mg <li><strong>Carbohydrates:</strong> 26.1g <li><strong>Fiber:</strong> 2.6g <li><strong>Protein:</strong> 3.8g</li></li></li></li></li></li></li></ul> </div>

<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 wpr_madethis_li" id="comment-857725">
<article id="article-comment-857725">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Kerri" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/94823dd8da06b1f8283fb607756f3958?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/94823dd8da06b1f8283fb607756f3958?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Kerri" width="96"><span itemprop="name">Kerri</span> <span class="says">says</span> </img></p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-857725">January 26, 2020 at 7:19 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>This recipe is amazing! I’ve been a vegetarian since childhood, but have recently been trying to transition to an entirely plant-based diet. I made this pizza for my sister, whose been vegan for about ten years, and my father, who eats anything. The pizza was a huge hit with everyone! The crust is flavorful and bakes up to a nice bread-like texture. Not flat and cracker-like, as you get with some gluten free recipes. I added pizza sauce, the home made ricotta cheese recipe that you included the link for (also  got rave reviews in and of itself), mushrooms, bell peppers, red onions, and spinach. The only issue I had, and this may have something to do with the fact that we live at sea level, is that the dough was way too wet using the proportions of the recipe, as written. But I just added more almond flour until it was the texture I wanted. I also baked the pizza on a tray, because it didn’t seem stable enough in just parchment. But it turned out beautifully.</p>
<div class="wprm-comment-rating">

<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hello! I’m so excited to try this recipe. I’ve got all the ingredients but want to know if I can prep the dough in the morning then cook in the evening. Can I just leave it in the fridge until I’m ready to bake? Thank you!!!</p>

<div class="comment-reply"><a aria-label="Reply to Jamie" class="comment-reply-link" data-belowelement="comment-829250" data-commentid="829250" data-postid="30757" data-respondelement="respond" href="#comment-829250" rel="nofollow">Reply</a></div>

<ul class="children">
<li class="comment byuser comment-author-support odd alt depth-2" id="comment-829263">
<article id="article-comment-829263">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Support @ Minimalist Baker" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/9501d522e8b6b56b741d5c9b17c76182?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/9501d522e8b6b56b741d5c9b17c76182?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Support @ Minimalist Baker" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Support @ Minimalist Baker</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-829263">September 20, 2019 at 8:45 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi Jamie, we haven’t tried that, so we aren’t completely sure. It may be okay to refrigerate, but the dough may not be quite as fluffy since the baking soda may lose some of its effectiveness. For best results, we would probably recommend par-baking it (doing the initial bake), and then freezing on a baking sheet and storing that way. Then bake as instructed, adding a little extra cooking time if baked from frozen. Let us know how it goes!</p>
</div>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi! I am making the crusts this morning (larger party coming over so making several pizzas) for dinner tonight. Should I still freeze the crusts and then pull out this evening for the remainder? Or would you just put them in the refrigerator at that point? It’s about a 7 hour difference from when the crusts will be ready to when I am putting on the toppings. Thank you!</p>

<div class="comment-reply"><a aria-label="Reply to Nicole Hughes" class="comment-reply-link" data-belowelement="comment-823587" data-commentid="823587" data-postid="30757" data-respondelement="respond" href="#comment-823587" rel="nofollow">Reply</a></div>

<li class="comment byuser comment-author-support odd alt depth-2" id="comment-823620">
<article id="article-comment-823620">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Support @ Minimalist Baker" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/9501d522e8b6b56b741d5c9b17c76182?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/9501d522e8b6b56b741d5c9b17c76182?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Support @ Minimalist Baker" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Support @ Minimalist Baker</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-823620">August 30, 2019 at 12:34 pm</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi Nicole, we haven’t tried that, so we aren’t completely sure. It may be okay to refrigerate, but the dough may not be quite as fluffy since the baking soda may lose some of its effectiveness. For best results, we would probably recommend par-baking it (doing the initial bake), and then freezing on a baking sheet and storing that way. Then bake as instructed, adding a little extra cooking time if baked from frozen. Let us know how it goes!</p>
</div>

<p>The picture I posted was a before picture. I was so starving and it looked so good that I couldn’t even wait to take an after. The crust is fantastic! I eat gluten because I am not allergic to it but this crust was so good with out it. It is SO easy to make! I bought marinara sauce to save me time, cut fresh veggies, and the Ricotta Cheese is a MUST! Thank you minimalist baker for always inspiring me to cook. I absolutely love cooking plant based and am a foodie so I had to share my experience since I appreciate all the honest feedback. &lt;3</p>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>Wow! Thank you so much for this recipe. Absolutely amazing crust. I have IBS and follow the low FODMAP diet, so I’ve been looking for a recipe that would work well for my sensitive and cranky tummy! I omitted the garlic powder (cannot digest garlic in any form) and used truffle-infused olive oil for some extra flavor! Also ran out of arrowroot partway through so I used some tapioca starch as well.  I topped with homemade tomato sauce and Tofutti Ricotta. So so delicious and look forward to eating this as leftovers tomorrow!</p>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>I substituted GF oat flour for the potato starch because I didn’t have any. I wouldn’t say it tasted like your traditional pizza crust (probably would be more traditional-tasting/fluffy with the potato starch, though), but I LOVE IT SO MUCH. I am pregnant and also allergic to everything and this is all I want to eat all day long. I’ve made it twice in the last five days. It’s nutty and yummy and I love it. Topped with roasted eggplant, sauteed onions/green peppers/mushroom, and a roasted red pepper sauce because I’m allergic to tomatoes. Thanks for existing, Dana!</p>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>I freaking love this recipe, man. I’ve made it several times, and the crust is absolutely perfect – crispy yet tender, and flavorful. Stands up to any toppings i toss st it. And who doesn’t love pizza?? </p>
<p>I’ve discovered a crust-spreading timesaver: Instead of dumping the lump of dough in the center of the parchment paper, I spoon it out, sort of as if I am making drop cookies. Then just connect the “cookies” to make a crust. Viola!</p>

<li class="comment even thread-even depth-1 wpr_madethis_li" id="comment-758945">
<article id="article-comment-758945">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Sara" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7eea27630352d1980f7d460d2c324b25?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7eea27630352d1980f7d460d2c324b25?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Sara" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Sara</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-758945">July 18, 2018 at 7:26 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>I made this last night. I loved it. Super fast and easy. I have made other gluten free, vegan crusts and this is so far the best. The popular cauliflower crust takes forever and other versions require too much advance prep. I substituted additional potato starch for the arrowroot starch and used coconut oil instead of olive. I also omitted the vinegar as I don’t use it.  It worked.<br/>
Pros: Super fast for last minute supper<br/>
          Easy to form a workable “dough” and easy to press or roll out<br/>
          Makes a crispy crust that really (really!) holds it’s shape<br/>
          I liked the taste (crumbly like an almond biscuit, not doughy like pizza dough)<br/>
Cons:  Some people might not like the consistency or flavor if looking for a real pizza<br/>
          dough feel. Tastes a bit like almond biscotti with a shortbread cookie<br/>
          consistency.<br/>
Ideas for next time: (Oh, there will be a next time!)<br/>
          This time I hand pressed it to 1/4inch thickness. I got a good size, 2-person pie.<br/>
          Next time I will roll it out thinner between two sheets of parchment. The crust<br/>
          flavor wont take over the pie and I will get twice the surface area. It is a strong<br/>
          crust and will really give a super thin crispy pizza feel.<br/>
          I will season the crust with additional herbs, parsley and thyme for a little<br/>
          extra tastebud appeal.<br/>
Thank you for this Godsend!!!  Now I won’t dread pizza night!</p>

<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Emily" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/fe6fa814bb73d919a55ca8d56e576932?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/fe6fa814bb73d919a55ca8d56e576932?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Emily" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Emily</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-758671">July 15, 2018 at 9:23 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>I have been making this crust about every other week (I know…!) since it was posted a few months ago. I love it’s simplicity – it reminds me of the simple mills gf crust in terms of ingredients and texture. However, it hurts my stomach quite a bit. There aren’t many filler flours in this crust in comparison to many other gf crusts I’ve tried. I knew it was the flax seed so I eliminated it and the texture of the crust really goes down hill and leftovers are basically cardboard. But! I substituted an EGG for the flax and it totally changed the texture of the crust and it’s great. Not to mention leftovers really hold up. The texture takes on a more doughy texture. I realize not everyone can eat egg or chooses not to, but if you can/want to and flax hurts your stomach, too, try adding 1 egg instead of flax (keep everything else the same). Game changer.</p>
<div class="wprm-comment-rating">

<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 wpr_madethis_li" id="comment-751136">
<article id="article-comment-751136">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Allie Moss" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/44c9145394ed7d7d1834172bd3d310cf?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/44c9145394ed7d7d1834172bd3d310cf?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Allie Moss" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Allie Moss</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-751136">April 29, 2018 at 6:54 pm</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>THANK YOU SO MUCH, DANA! I’d given up, but after 6 years of being gluten and dairy free, you have given me a pizza that is easy and delicious and not overprocessed. The almond whipped ricotta (I made a half recipe) is perfection on this.</p>
<p>I made your recipe without modifications a couple weeks ago. But I was craving it again this past week and didn’t have arrowroot on hand, so I tried tapioca as suggested as a possible sub previously. It came out great! I’ll still stick to arrowroot when I have it but I wanted to comment to let others know that tapioca worked for me.</p>
<p>Also! The whole pizza is 4 servings for me, so second time ’round I made 2 smaller pizzas. One crust, I parbaked and froze. The other, I cooked up and had half hot and half the next day cold. It was great all the ways.</p>

<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 wpr_madethis_li" id="comment-748964">
<article id="article-comment-748964">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Sam Watson" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/c74017c372e412e0aeab42e91574caa8?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/c74017c372e412e0aeab42e91574caa8?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Sam Watson" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Sam Watson</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-748964">April 7, 2018 at 5:30 pm</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>I made this dough almost exactly as stated and it turned out great. I will admit that I may have left the dough a littler thicker than 1/4 an inch but not by much and I broiled on high for the last 4 minutes. I also ran out of parchment paper so I cooked it on a sheet pan. This dough is rich and will definitely fill you up. It’s tasty, crisp on the edges and tender on the inside. I put store bought marinara on top with onions, peppers, kalmata olives and mushrooms. I topped with salt, evoo and yeast seasoning. My dad (who eats only junk food) and my husband (not gluten free) loved this and so did I! Will definitely make again; it was so easy! Thanks for this!</p>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>I’ve been making the same vegan GF pizza crust for years but decided to try this because it looked easy and because I’ve had success with so many recipes on this site. After the initial bake I knew I could never pass this off as pizza crust to my kids, so chose not to make it into a pizza. It’s more of a nutty, crumbly, biscuit-y flatbread. Tastes okay but not like traditional pizza crust at all. Will enjoy it as bread to accompany soup.</p>
</div>

<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-746641">March 16, 2018 at 3:01 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Hi Dana!<br/>
Thanks for the recipe. But in ingredients, you say “almond flour not almond meal”. What’s the difference?</p>
</div>
<div class="comment-reply"><a aria-label="Reply to ginebra" class="comment-reply-link" data-belowelement="comment-746641" data-commentid="746641" data-postid="30757" data-respondelement="respond" href="#comment-746641" rel="nofollow">Reply</a></div>
</article>
<ul class="children">
<li class="comment byuser comment-author-dana bypostauthor odd alt depth-2" id="comment-746655">
<article id="article-comment-746655">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Dana @ Minimalist Baker" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/c7caa94d71e10eb485999d00c6e9b624?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/c7caa94d71e10eb485999d00c6e9b624?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Dana @ Minimalist Baker" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Dana @ Minimalist Baker</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-746655">March 16, 2018 at 8:05 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Almond flour is made from blanched almonds with the skin removed. Almond meal is made from whole raw ground almonds. The almond flour yields a fluffier texture and more delicate flavor.</p>
</div>
<div class="comment-reply"><a aria-label="Reply to Dana @ Minimalist Baker" class="comment-reply-link" data-belowelement="comment-746655" data-commentid="746655" data-postid="30757" data-respondelement="respond" href="#comment-746655" rel="nofollow">Reply</a></div>
</article>

<li class="comment odd alt depth-3 wpr_madethis_li" id="comment-746909">

<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Hilary" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/048b214e2936461b1106ff3222b9507f?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/048b214e2936461b1106ff3222b9507f?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Hilary" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Hilary</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-746909">March 18, 2018 at 12:12 pm</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Thank you, Dana!  When I posted my question, I was thinking for some reason that all we needed of the starches was 1/2 tsp, not 1/2 cup.  Measurement makes a difference… ;) </p>
<p>Made this yesterday and it worked nicely – it felt almost like a yeasted dough.  I used oat flour in place of almond; potato flour in place of starch; and tapioca flour in place of arrowroot starch.  (I already had the potato and tapioca flours on hand.)  It took 16 or 17 tbsp of water, but I think different flours are more thirsty than others.</p>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>I make my own hazelnut flour by blending the raw nuts in the blender till they  are fine and then perhaps put them through a sieve but i do not mind them a bit grainy. Just use small amounts so the pieces fly around right on top speed. That is my experience also with cashews and other nuts.</p>
</div>

<li class="comment even depth-4" id="comment-767806">
<article id="article-comment-767806">
<header class="comment-header">
<p class="comment-author">
<img alt="Avatar for Jane" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/007f7fc0d31372b3b56b67a9b919fa8b?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/007f7fc0d31372b3b56b67a9b919fa8b?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Jane" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Jane</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-767806">October 3, 2018 at 6:58 pm</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>Love this recipe!</p>
<p>I make my own almond flour by first making almond milk. Soak a half cup of  raw almonds overnight and slip off the skins. I use the tall unit of a Nutribullet to grind the soaked almonds with purified water up to the max fill line then strain out the pulp with a nut milk bag. Crumble out the remaining pulp after squeezing out the milk onto a dehydrator fruit roll sheet and dehydrate till dry. Then grind to a fine flour in the small unit of the Nutribullet et volia almond flour!</p>

<img alt="Avatar for Christina" class="avatar avatar-96 photo" height="96" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/2947b5920289ec4deba748e08ed35d5a?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/2947b5920289ec4deba748e08ed35d5a?s=192&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" title="Gravatar for Christina" width="96"/><span itemprop="name">Christina</span> <span class="says">says</span> </p>
<p class="comment-meta"><time class="comment-time"><a class="comment-time-link" href="https://minimalistbaker.com/easy-vegan-gluten-free-pizza-crust/?t=1582420901#comment-748163">March 31, 2018 at 2:47 am</a></time></p> </header>
<div class="comment-content">
<p>I use the vita mix with the ssd’s special grain/nut mill blender you can order from them. It works awesome. You can also do with the standard blender just do short pulses repeatedly, allowing the notes to settle in between pulses, and dont over do it. There’s a fine line between flour and nut butter.</p>
</div>

<div class="comment-content">
<p>This recipe looks delicious. My son is potato and rice intolerant and I’m gluten intolerant. This makes it complicated, as you can imagine. I’ve recently discovered almond flour and I love the added flavor it brings. I find much of the gluten free products to be so pasty. Anyway, in your experience can you recommend another starch besides potato that might work? Corn? Tapioca?  I’m reluctant to experiment for fear of wasting good food so I like to rely on other people‘s experiments whenever possible. : )</p>
</div>

					function mgclInit() {
						if (jQuery.fn.off) {
							jQuery('.no-lightbox, .no-lightbox img').off('click'); // jQuery 1.7+
						}
						else {
							jQuery('.no-lightbox, .no-lightbox img').unbind('click'); // < jQuery 1.7
						}
						jQuery('a.no-lightbox').click(mgclOnClick);

						if (jQuery.fn.off) {
							jQuery('a.set-target').off('click'); // jQuery 1.7+
						}
						else {
							jQuery('a.set-target').unbind('click'); // < jQuery 1.7
						}
						jQuery('a.set-target').click(mgclOnClick);
					}

					function mgclOnClick() {
						if (!this.target || this.target == '' || this.target == '_self')
							window.location = this.href;
						else
							window.open(this.href,this.target);
						return false;
					}

					// From WP Gallery Custom Links
					// Reduce the number of  conflicting lightboxes
					function mgclAddLoadEvent(func) {
						var oldOnload = window.onload;
						if (typeof window.onload != 'function') {
							window.onload = func;
						} else {
							window.onload = function() {
								oldOnload();
								func();
							}
						}
					}

					mgclAddLoadEvent(mgclInit);
					mgclInit();

				});
